users of these terms contend that using the official name of the region would imply acceptance of the legitimacy of the Government of Ireland Act.</li>\n<li><b>The Occupied Six Counties</b> \xe2\x80\x93 used by some republicans.<sup id="cite_ref-87" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-87">&#91;87&#93;</a></sup> The Republic, whose legitimacy is similarly not recognised by republicans opposed to the Belfast Agreement, is described as the "Free State", referring to the <a href="/wiki/Irish_Free_State" title="Irish Free State">Irish Free State</a>, which gained independence (as a <a href="/wiki/Dominion" title="Dominion">Dominion</a>) in 1922.<sup id="cite_ref-88" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-88">&#91;88&#93;</a></sup></li>\n<li><b>British-Occupied Ireland</b> \xe2\x80\x93 Similar in tone to the Occupied Six Counties,<sup id="cite_ref-89" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-89">&#91;89&#93;</a></sup> this term is used by more dogmatic republicans, such as <a href="/wiki/Republican_Sinn_F%C3%A9in" title="Republican Sinn F\xc3\xa9in">Republican Sinn F\xc3\xa9in</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-90" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-90">&#91;90&#93;</a></sup> who still hold that the <a href="/wiki/Second_D%C3%A1il" title="Second D\xc3\xa1il">Second D\xc3\xa1il</a> was the last legitimate government of Ireland and that all governments since have been foreign-imposed usurpations of Irish national self-determination.<sup id="cite_ref-91" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-91">&#91;91&#93;</a></sup></li></ul>\n<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Other">Other</span></h4>\n<ul><li><b>Norn Iron</b> or "Norniron" \xe2\x80\x93 is an informal and affectionate<sup id="cite_ref-92" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-92">&#91;92&#93;</a></sup> local nickname used by both nationalists<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (December 2015)">citation needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup> and unionists to refer to Northern Ireland, derived from the pronunciation of the words "Northern Ireland" in an exaggerated Ulster accent (particularly one from the greater Belfast area). The phrase is seen as a lighthearted way to refer to Northern Ireland, based as it is on regional pronunciation. It often refers to the <a href="/wiki/Northern_Ireland_national_football_team" title="Northern Ireland national football team">Northern Ireland national football team</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-93" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-93">&#91;93&#93;</a></sup></li></ul>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Geography_and_climate">Geography and climate</span></h2>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main articles: <a href="/wiki/Geography_of_Ireland" title="Geography of Ireland">Geography of Ireland</a> and <a href="/wiki/Geography_of_the_United_Kingdom" title="Geography of the United Kingdom">Geography of the United Kingdom</a></div>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Northern_Ireland_K%C3%B6ppen.png" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/44/Northern_Ireland_K%C3%B6ppen.png/220px-Northern_Ireland_K%C3%B6ppen.png" width="220" height="264" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/44/Northern_Ireland_K%C3%B6ppen.png/330px-Northern_Ireland_K%C3%B6ppen.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/44/Northern_Ireland_K%C3%B6ppen.png/440px-Northern_Ireland_K%C3%B6ppen.png 2x" data-file-width="5400" data-file-height="6481" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Northern_Ireland_K%C3%B6ppen.png" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/K%C3%B6ppen_climate_classification" title="K\xc3\xb6ppen climate classification">K\xc3\xb6ppen climate types</a> of Northern Ireland</div></div></div>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Lough_Neagh_-_geograph.org.uk_-_488526.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0c/Lough_Neagh_-_geograph.org.uk_-_488526.jpg/220px-Lough_Neagh_-_geograph.org.uk_-_488526.jpg" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0c/Lough_Neagh_-_geograph.org.uk_-_488526.jpg/330px-Lough_Neagh_-_geograph.org.uk_-_488526.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0c/Lough_Neagh_-_geograph.org.uk_-_488526.jpg/440px-Lough_Neagh_-_geograph.org.uk_-_488526.jpg 2x" data-file-width="640" data-file-height="480" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Lough_Neagh_-_geograph.org.uk_-_488526.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Lough_Neagh" title="Lough Neagh">Lough Neagh</a></div></div></div>\n<p>Northern Ireland was covered by an <a href="/wiki/Ice_sheet" title="Ice sheet">ice sheet</a> for most of the <a href="/wiki/Quaternary_glaciation" title="Quaternary glaciation">last ice age</a> and on numerous previous occasions, the legacy of which can be seen in the extensive coverage of <a href="/wiki/Drumlin" title="Drumlin">drumlins</a> in Counties Fermanagh, Armagh, Antrim and particularly Down.\n</p><p>The centrepiece of Northern Ireland\'s geography is <a href="/wiki/Lough_Neagh" title="Lough Neagh">Lough Neagh</a>, at 151 square miles (391&#160;km<sup>2</sup>) the largest freshwater lake both on the island of Ireland and in the <a href="/wiki/British_Isles" title="British Isles">British Isles</a>. A second extensive lake system is centred on Lower and Upper <a href="/wiki/Lough_Erne" title="Lough Erne">Lough Erne</a> in Fermanagh. The largest island of Northern Ireland is <a href="/wiki/Rathlin_Island" title="Rathlin Island">Rathlin</a>, off the north Antrim coast. <a href="/wiki/Strangford_Lough" title="Strangford Lough">Strangford Lough</a> is the largest inlet in the British Isles, covering 150&#160;km<sup>2</sup> (58&#160;sq&#160;mi).\n</p>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Hare%27s_Gap_-_geograph.org.uk_-_66827.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6b/Hare%27s_Gap_-_geograph.org.uk_-_66827.jpg/220px-Hare%27s_Gap_-_geograph.org.uk_-_66827.jpg" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6b/Hare%27s_Gap_-_geograph.org.uk_-_66827.jpg/330px-Hare%27s_Gap_-_geograph.org.uk_-_66827.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6b/Hare%27s_Gap_-_geograph.org.uk_-_66827.jpg/440px-Hare%27s_Gap_-_geograph.org.uk_-_66827.jpg 2x" data-file-width="640" data-file-height="479" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Hare%27s_Gap_-_geograph.org.uk_-_66827.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Hare\'s Gap, <a href="/wiki/Mourne_Mountains" title="Mourne Mountains">Mourne Mountains</a></div></div></div>\n<p>There are substantial uplands in the <a href="/wiki/Sperrin_Mountains" class="mw-redirect" title="Sperrin Mountains">Sperrin Mountains</a> (an extension of the <a href="/wiki/Caledonian_orogeny" title="Caledonian orogeny">Caledonian mountain belt</a>) with extensive gold deposits, <a href="/wiki/Granite" title="Granite">granite</a> <a href="/wiki/Mourne_Mountains" title="Mourne Mountains">Mourne Mountains</a> and <a href="/wiki/Basalt" title="Basalt">basalt</a> <a href="/wiki/Antrim_Plateau" class="mw-redirect" title="Antrim Plateau">Antrim Plateau</a>, as well as smaller ranges in <a href="/wiki/County_Armagh" title="County Armagh">South Armagh</a> and along the Fermanagh\xe2\x80\x93Tyrone border. None of the hills are especially high, with <a href="/wiki/Slieve_Donard" title="Slieve Donard">Slieve Donard</a> in the dramatic Mournes reaching 850 metres (2,789&#160;ft), Northern Ireland\'s highest point. Belfast\'s most prominent peak is <a href="/wiki/Cavehill" title="Cavehill">Cavehill</a>.\n</p>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Causeway-code_poet-4.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c0/Causeway-code_poet-4.jpg/220px-Causeway-code_poet-4.jpg" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c0/Causeway-code_poet-4.jpg/330px-Causeway-code_poet-4.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c0/Causeway-code_poet-4.jpg/440px-Causeway-code_poet-4.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2048" data-file-height="1536" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Causeway-code_poet-4.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The <a href="/wiki/Giant%27s_Causeway" title="Giant&#39;s Causeway">Giant\'s Causeway</a>, <a href="/wiki/County_Antrim" title="County Antrim">County Antrim</a></div></div></div>\n<p>The volcanic activity which created the Antrim Plateau also formed the eerily geometric pillars of the <a href="/wiki/Giant%27s_Causeway" title="Giant&#39;s Causeway">Giant\'s Causeway</a> on the north Antrim coast. Also in north Antrim are the <a href="/wiki/Carrick-a-Rede_Rope_Bridge" title="Carrick-a-Rede Rope Bridge">Carrick-a-Rede Rope Bridge</a>, <a href="/wiki/Mussenden_Temple" title="Mussenden Temple">Mussenden Temple</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Glens_of_Antrim" title="Glens of Antrim">Glens of Antrim</a>.\n</p>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Marble_Arch_Caves_-_Skreen_Hill_streamway.jpeg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b8/Marble_Arch_Caves_-_Skreen_Hill_streamway.jpeg/220px-Marble_Arch_Caves_-_Skreen_Hill_streamway.jpeg" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b8/Marble_Arch_Caves_-_Skreen_Hill_streamway.jpeg/330px-Marble_Arch_Caves_-_Skreen_Hill_streamway.jpeg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b8/Marble_Arch_Caves_-_Skreen_Hill_streamway.jpeg/440px-Marble_Arch_Caves_-_Skreen_Hill_streamway.jpeg 2x" data-file-width="2592" data-file-height="1944" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Marble_Arch_Caves_-_Skreen_Hill_streamway.jpeg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Marble_Arch_Caves" title="Marble Arch Caves">Marble Arch Caves</a></div></div></div>\n<p>The Lower and Upper <a href="/wiki/River_Bann" title="River Bann">River Bann</a>, <a href="/wiki/River_Foyle" title="River Foyle">River Foyle</a> and <a href="/wiki/River_Blackwater,_Northern_Ireland" class="mw-redirect" title="River Blackwater, Northern Ireland">River Blackwater</a> form extensive fertile lowlands, with excellent <a href="/wiki/Arable_land" title="Arable land">arable land</a> also found in North and East Down, although much of the hill country is marginal and suitable largely for animal husbandry.\n</p><p>The valley of the <a href="/wiki/River_Lagan" title="River Lagan">River Lagan</a> is dominated by Belfast, whose metropolitan area includes over a third of the population of Northern Ireland, with heavy urbanisation and industrialisation along the Lagan Valley and both shores of <a href="/wiki/Belfast_Lough" title="Belfast Lough">Belfast Lough</a>.\n</p><p>The whole of Northern Ireland has a <a href="/wiki/Maritime_climate" class="mw-redirect" title="Maritime climate">temperate maritime climate</a>, rather wetter in the west than the east, although cloud cover is persistent across the region. The weather is unpredictable at all times of the year, and although the seasons are distinct, they are considerably less pronounced than in interior Europe or the eastern seaboard of North America. Average daytime maximums in Belfast are 6.5&#160;\xc2\xb0C (43.7&#160;\xc2\xb0F) in January and 17.5&#160;\xc2\xb0C (63.5&#160;\xc2\xb0F) in July. The highest maximum temperature recorded was 30.8&#160;\xc2\xb0C (87.4&#160;\xc2\xb0F) at Knockarevan, near <a href="/wiki/Garrison,_County_Fermanagh" title="Garrison, County Fermanagh">Garrison, County Fermanagh</a> on 30 June 1976 and at Belfast on 12 July 1983.<sup id="cite_ref-94" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-94">&#91;94&#93;</a></sup> The lowest minimum temperature recorded was \xe2\x88\x9218.7&#160;\xc2\xb0C (\xe2\x88\x921.7&#160;\xc2\xb0F) at <a href="/wiki/Castlederg" title="Castlederg">Castlederg</a>, <a href="/wiki/County_Tyrone" title="County Tyrone">County Tyrone</a> on 23 December 2010.<sup id="cite_ref-MetO2010-12_95-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-MetO2010-12-95">&#91;95&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Counties">Counties</span></h3>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Counties_of_Northern_Ireland" title="Counties of Northern Ireland">Counties of Northern Ireland</a></div>\n<p>Northern Ireland consists of six historic <a href="/wiki/Counties_of_Ireland" title="Counties of Ireland">counties</a>: <a href="/wiki/County_Antrim" title="County Antrim">County Antrim</a>, <a href="/wiki/County_Armagh" title="County Armagh">County Armagh</a>, <a href="/wiki/County_Down" title="County Down">County Down</a>, <a href="/wiki/County_Fermanagh" title="County Fermanagh">County Fermanagh</a>, <a href="/wiki/County_Londonderry" title="County Londonderry">County Londonderry</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-96" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-96">&#91;96&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/County_Tyrone" title="County Tyrone">County Tyrone</a>.\n</p><p>These counties are no longer used for local government purposes; instead, there are eleven <a href="/wiki/Districts_of_Northern_Ireland" class="mw-redirect" title="Districts of Northern Ireland">districts of Northern Ireland</a> which have different geographical extents. These were created in 2015, replacing the twenty-six districts which previously existed.<sup id="cite_ref-97" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-97">&#91;97&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:MussendenTemple.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1f/MussendenTemple.jpg/220px-MussendenTemple.jpg" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1f/MussendenTemple.jpg/330px-MussendenTemple.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1f/MussendenTemple.jpg/440px-MussendenTemple.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2592" data-file-height="1944" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:MussendenTemple.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Mussenden_Temple" title="Mussenden Temple">Mussenden Temple</a>, <a href="/wiki/County_Londonderry" title="County Londonderry">County Londonderry</a></div></div></div>\n<p>Although counties are no longer used for local governmental purposes, they remain a popular means of describing where places are. They are officially used while applying for an <a href="/wiki/Irish_passport" title="Irish passport">Irish passport</a>, which requires one to state one\'s county of birth. The name of that county then appears in both Irish and English on the passport\'s information page, as opposed to the town or city of birth on the United Kingdom passport. The <a href="/wiki/Gaelic_Athletic_Association" title="Gaelic Athletic Association">Gaelic Athletic Association</a> still uses the counties as its primary means of organisation and fields representative teams of each <a href="/wiki/GAA_county" class="mw-redirect" title="GAA county">GAA county</a>. The original system of <a href="/wiki/License_plates_of_Northern_Ireland" class="mw-redirect" title="License plates of Northern Ireland">car registration numbers</a> largely based on counties still remains in use. In 2000, the <a href="/wiki/Big_Number_Change#Northern_Ireland" title="Big Number Change">telephone numbering system</a> was restructured into an 8 digit scheme with (except for Belfast) the first digit approximately reflecting the county.\n</p><p>The county boundaries still appear on Ordnance Survey of Northern Ireland Maps and the Phillips Street Atlases, among others. With their decline in official use, there is often confusion surrounding towns and cities which lie near county boundaries, such as Belfast and <a href="/wiki/Lisburn" title="Lisburn">Lisburn</a>, which are split between counties Down and Antrim (the majorities of both cities, however, are in Antrim).\n</p><p>In March 2018, <i>The Sunday Times</i> published its list of Best Places to Live in Britain, including the following places in Northern Ireland: Ballyhackamore near Belfast (overall best for Northern Ireland), Holywood, County Down, Newcastle, County Down, Portrush, County Antrim, Strangford, County Down.<sup id="cite_ref-98" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-98">&#91;98&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Economy">Economy</span></h2>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main articles: <a href="/wiki/Economy_of_Northern_Ireland" title="Economy of Northern Ireland">Economy of Northern Ireland</a> and <a href="/wiki/Transport_in_Northern_Ireland" class="mw-redirect" title="Transport in Northern Ireland">Transport in Northern Ireland</a></div>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:%27Titanic_Quarter%27_development,_Abercorn_Basin,_Belfast_-_geograph.org.uk_-_1378153.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2c/%27Titanic_Quarter%27_development%2C_Abercorn_Basin%2C_Belfast_-_geograph.org.uk_-_1378153.jpg/220px-%27Titanic_Quarter%27_development%2C_Abercorn_Basin%2C_Belfast_-_geograph.org.uk_-_1378153.jpg" width="220" height="161" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2c/%27Titanic_Quarter%27_development%2C_Abercorn_Basin%2C_Belfast_-_geograph.org.uk_-_1378153.jpg/330px-%27Titanic_Quarter%27_development%2C_Abercorn_Basin%2C_Belfast_-_geograph.org.uk_-_1378153.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2c/%27Titanic_Quarter%27_development%2C_Abercorn_Basin%2C_Belfast_-_geograph.org.uk_-_1378153.jpg/440px-%27Titanic_Quarter%27_development%2C_Abercorn_Basin%2C_Belfast_-_geograph.org.uk_-_1378153.jpg 2x" data-file-width="640" data-file-height="468" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:%27Titanic_Quarter%27_development,_Abercorn_Basin,_Belfast_-_geograph.org.uk_-_1378153.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Goliath crane of <a href="/wiki/Harland_%26_Wolff" class="mw-redirect" title="Harland &amp; Wolff">Harland &amp; Wolff</a> in <a href="/wiki/Belfast" title="Belfast">Belfast</a>.</div></div></div>\n<p>Northern Ireland has traditionally had an industrial economy, most notably in shipbuilding, rope manufacture and textiles, but most heavy industry has since been replaced by services, primarily the public sector. Government subsidies account for 20% of the economy\'s revenue.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (January 2016)">citation needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup>\n</p><p>Seventy percent of the economy\'s revenue comes from the service sector. Apart from the public sector, another important service sector is tourism, which rose to account for over 1% of the economy\'s revenue in 2004. Tourism has been a major growth area since the end of the Troubles. Key tourism attractions include the historic cities of Derry, Belfast and <a href="/wiki/Armagh" title="Armagh">Armagh</a> and the many castles in Northern Ireland. More recently, the economy has benefited from major investment by many large multi-national corporations into high tech industry.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (January 2016)">citation needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup> These large firms are attracted by government subsidies and the skilled workforce in Northern Ireland.\n</p><p>The local economy has seen contraction during the <a href="/wiki/Great_Recession" title="Great Recession">Great Recession</a>. In response, the Northern Ireland Assembly has sent trade missions abroad. The Executive wishes to gain taxation powers from London, to align Northern Ireland\'s <a href="/wiki/Corporation_tax" class="mw-redirect" title="Corporation tax">corporation tax</a> rate with the unusually low rate of the Republic of Ireland.\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Transport">Transport</span></h2>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Transport_in_Northern_Ireland" class="mw-redirect" title="Transport in Northern Ireland">Transport in Northern Ireland</a></div>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Approaching_Seahill_station_-_geograph.org.uk_-_243422.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b6/Approaching_Seahill_station_-_geograph.org.uk_-_243422.jpg/220px-Approaching_Seahill_station_-_geograph.org.uk_-_243422.jpg" width="220" height="146" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b6/Approaching_Seahill_station_-_geograph.org.uk_-_243422.jpg/330px-Approaching_Seahill_station_-_geograph.org.uk_-_243422.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b6/Approaching_Seahill_station_-_geograph.org.uk_-_243422.jpg/440px-Approaching_Seahill_station_-_geograph.org.uk_-_243422.jpg 2x" data-file-width="640" data-file-height="426" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Approaching_Seahill_station_-_geograph.org.uk_-_243422.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>An <a href="/wiki/Northern_Ireland_Railways" class="mw-redirect" title="Northern Ireland Railways">NIR</a> <a href="/wiki/NIR_Class_3000" title="NIR Class 3000">C3K</a> <a href="/wiki/Railcar" title="Railcar">railcar</a></div></div></div>\n<p>Northern Ireland has underdeveloped <a href="/wiki/Transport_in_Northern_Ireland" class="mw-redirect" title="Transport in Northern Ireland">transport infrastructure</a>, with most infrastructure concentrated around Greater Belfast, Greater Derry and Craigavon.  Northern Ireland is served by three airports \xe2\x80\x93 <a href="/wiki/Belfast_International_Airport" title="Belfast International Airport">Belfast International</a> near <a href="/wiki/Antrim,_County_Antrim" title="Antrim, County Antrim">Antrim</a>, <a href="/wiki/George_Best_Belfast_City_Airport" title="George Best Belfast City Airport">George Best Belfast City</a> integrated into the railway network at <a href="/wiki/Sydenham_railway_station,_Northern_Ireland" class="mw-redirect" title="Sydenham railway station, Northern Ireland">Sydenham</a> in East Belfast, and <a href="/wiki/City_of_Derry_Airport" title="City of Derry Airport">City of Derry</a> in County Londonderry.\n</p><p>Major seaports at <a href="/wiki/Larne" title="Larne">Larne</a> and <a href="/wiki/Port_of_Belfast" class="mw-redirect" title="Port of Belfast">Belfast</a> carry passengers and freight between Great Britain and Northern Ireland.\n</p><p>Passenger railways are operated by <a href="/wiki/Northern_Ireland_Railways" class="mw-redirect" title="Northern Ireland Railways">Northern Ireland Railways</a>. With <a href="/wiki/Iarnr%C3%B3d_%C3%89ireann" title="Iarnr\xc3\xb3d \xc3\x89ireann">Iarnr\xc3\xb3d \xc3\x89ireann</a> (Irish Rail), <a href="/wiki/Northern_Ireland_Railways" class="mw-redirect" title="Northern Ireland Railways">Northern Ireland Railways</a> co-operates in providing the joint <a href="/wiki/Enterprise_(train)" class="mw-redirect" title="Enterprise (train)">Enterprise</a> service between <a href="/wiki/Dublin_Connolly" class="mw-redirect" title="Dublin Connolly">Dublin Connolly</a> and <a href="/wiki/Lanyon_Place_railway_station" title="Lanyon Place railway station">Lanyon Place</a>. The whole of Ireland has a mainline railway network with a <a href="/wiki/Track_gauge_in_Ireland" title="Track gauge in Ireland">gauge of 5&#160;ft 3&#160;in (1,600&#160;mm)</a>, which is unique in Europe and has resulted in distinct rolling stock designs. The only preserved line of this gauge is the <a href="/wiki/Downpatrick_and_County_Down_Railway" title="Downpatrick and County Down Railway">Downpatrick and County Down Railway</a>. Main railway lines linking to and from <a href="/wiki/Belfast_Great_Victoria_Street_railway_station" title="Belfast Great Victoria Street railway station">Belfast Great Victoria Street railway station</a> and <a href="/wiki/Belfast_Central_railway_station" class="mw-redirect" title="Belfast Central railway station">Belfast Central</a> are:\n</p>\n<ul><li>The <a href="/wiki/Belfast%E2%80%93Derry_railway_line" class="mw-redirect" title="Belfast\xe2\x80\x93Derry railway line">Derry Line</a> and the Portrush Branch.</li>\n<li>The Larne Line</li>\n<li>The Bangor Line</li>\n<li>The <a href="/wiki/Portadown_railway_station" title="Portadown railway station">Portadown</a> Line</li></ul>\n<p>Main motorways are:\n</p>\n<ul><li><a href="/wiki/M1_motorway_(Northern_Ireland)" title="M1 motorway (Northern Ireland)">M1</a> connecting Belfast to the south and west, ending in <a href="/wiki/Dungannon" title="Dungannon">Dungannon</a></li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/M12_motorway_(Northern_Ireland)" class="mw-redirect" title="M12 motorway (Northern Ireland)">M12</a> connecting the <a href="/wiki/M1_motorway_(Northern_Ireland)" title="M1 motorway (Northern Ireland)">M1</a> to <a href="/wiki/Portadown" title="Portadown">Portadown</a></li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/M2_motorway_(Northern_Ireland)" title="M2 motorway (Northern Ireland)">M2</a> connecting Belfast to the north.  An unconnected section of the <a href="/wiki/M2_motorway_(Northern_Ireland)" title="M2 motorway (Northern Ireland)">M2</a> also by-passes <a href="/wiki/Ballymena" title="Ballymena">Ballymena</a></li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/M22_motorway_(Northern_Ireland)" title="M22 motorway (Northern Ireland)">M22</a> connecting the <a href="/wiki/M2_motorway_(Northern_Ireland)" title="M2 motorway (Northern Ireland)">M2</a> to near <a href="/wiki/Randalstown" title="Randalstown">Randalstown</a></li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/M3_motorway_(Northern_Ireland)" title="M3 motorway (Northern Ireland)">M3</a> connecting the M1 and M2 in Belfast with the A2 dual carriageway to <a href="/wiki/Bangor,_County_Down" title="Bangor, County Down">Bangor</a></li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/M5_motorway_(Northern_Ireland)" title="M5 motorway (Northern Ireland)">M5</a> connecting Belfast to <a href="/wiki/Newtownabbey" title="Newtownabbey">Newtownabbey</a></li></ul>\n<p>The cross-border road connecting the ports of <a href="/wiki/Larne" title="Larne">Larne</a> in Northern Ireland and <a href="/wiki/Rosslare_Harbour" title="Rosslare Harbour">Rosslare Harbour</a> in the Republic of Ireland is being upgraded as part of an EU-funded scheme. <a href="/wiki/European_route_E01" title="European route E01">European route E01</a> runs from Larne through the island of Ireland, Spain and Portugal to <a href="/wiki/Seville" title="Seville">Seville</a>.\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Demographics">Demographics</span></h2>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main articles: <a href="/wiki/Demography_of_Northern_Ireland" title="Demography of Northern Ireland">Demography of Northern Ireland</a>, <a href="/wiki/People_of_Northern_Ireland" title="People of Northern Ireland">People of Northern Ireland</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Religion_in_Northern_Ireland" title="Religion in Northern Ireland">Religion in Northern Ireland</a></div>\n<div class="barbox tright" style="overflow-x: auto;">\n<div style="border:1px solid silver; font-size:88%; padding:0.4em; width:auto; background: white;">\n<table style="text-align:left; border-collapse:collapse; width:100%;">\n<tbody><tr style="background:#ddd"><th style="text-align:center;" colspan="5">Religion in Northern Ireland \xe2\x80\x93 2011</th></tr>\n<tr style="font-size:88%; height:4px;">\n<td style="padding:0 4px; text-align:left;">Religion</td>\n<td style="padding:0 4px; text-align:right;"></td>\n<td right;">0.8%</td>\n</tr>\n\n</tbody></table>\n</div>\n</div>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Religion_or_religion_brought_up_in.png" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3a/Religion_or_religion_brought_up_in.png/220px-Religion_or_religion_brought_up_in.png" width="220" height="171" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3a/Religion_or_religion_brought_up_in.png/330px-Religion_or_religion_brought_up_in.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3a/Religion_or_religion_brought_up_in.png/440px-Religion_or_religion_brought_up_in.png 2x" data-file-width="19059" data-file-height="14839" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Religion_or_religion_brought_up_in.png" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>2011 census: differences in proportions of those who are, or were brought up, either Catholic or Protestant/Other Christians</div></div></div>\n<p>The population of Northern Ireland has risen yearly since 1978. The population in 2011 was 1.8&#160;million, having grown 7.5% over the previous decade<sup id="cite_ref-Census_2011_99-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Census_2011-99">&#91;99&#93;</a></sup> from just under 1.7&#160;million in 2001. This constitutes just under 3% of the population of the UK (62&#160;million) and just over 28% of the population of the island of Ireland (6.3&#160;million).\n</p><p>The population of Northern Ireland is almost entirely <a href="/wiki/White_people" title="White people">white</a> (98.2%).<sup id="cite_ref-Census_2011_99-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Census_2011-99">&#91;99&#93;</a></sup> In 2011, 88.8% of the population were born in Northern Ireland, with 4.5% born in Britain, and 2.9% born in the Republic of Ireland. 4.3% were born elsewhere; triple the amount there were in 2001.<sup id="cite_ref-100" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-100">&#91;100&#93;</a></sup> Most are from Eastern Europe and <a href="/wiki/Lithuania" title="Lithuania">Lithuania</a> and <a href="/wiki/Latvia" title="Latvia">Latvia</a>. The largest non-white ethnic groups were <a href="/wiki/Overseas_Chinese" title="Overseas Chinese">Chinese</a> (6,300) and <a href="/wiki/Non-resident_Indian_and_person_of_Indian_origin" title="Non-resident Indian and person of Indian origin">Indian</a> (6,200). <a href="/wiki/Black_people" title="Black people">Black people</a> of various origins made up 0.2% of the 2011 population and people of mixed ethnicity made up 0.2%.<sup id="cite_ref-ReferenceA_101-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ReferenceA-101">&#91;101&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Religion">Religion</span></h3>\n<p>At the 2011 census, 41.5% of the population identified as Protestant/non-Roman Catholic Christian, the biggest of these denominations being the <a href="/wiki/Presbyterian_Church_in_Ireland" title="Presbyterian Church in Ireland">Presbyterian Church</a> (19%), the <a href="/wiki/Church_of_Ireland" title="Church of Ireland">Church of Ireland</a> (14%) and the <a href="/wiki/Methodist_Church_in_Ireland" title="Methodist Church in Ireland">Methodist Church</a> (3%),  41% as <a href="/wiki/Roman_Catholicism_in_Ireland" class="mw-redirect" title="Roman Catholicism in Ireland">Roman Catholic</a>, and 0.8% as non-Christian, while 17% identified with no religion or did not state one.<sup id="cite_ref-ReferenceA_101-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ReferenceA-101">&#91;101&#93;</a></sup> In terms of community background (i.e. religion or religion brought up in), 48% of the population came from a Protestant background, 45% from a Catholic background, 0.9% from non-Christian backgrounds, and 5.6% from non-religious backgrounds.<sup id="cite_ref-ReferenceA_101-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ReferenceA-101">&#91;101&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<div style="clear:both;"></div>\n<table class="infobox" style="text-align:center; width:97%; margin-right:10px;
